{"type":"user","message":{"role":"user","content":[{"tool_use_id":"call_3a5e1540ba1b46db95599291","type":"tool_result","content":"1\t# bead-forge Implementation Plan\n2\t\n3\t## Overview\n4\t\n5\t**bead-forge** (`bf`) is a Rust binary that replaces `br` (beads_rust). SQLite is the live database — all reads and writes go through it. `issues.jsonl` is a git-synced artifact exported on demand: one entry per bead, committed to the repo for backup, sharing, and recovery. Concurrent claiming is handled by SQLite's `BEGIN IMMEDIATE` transaction — no server, no daemon, no flock required.\n6\t\n7\t## Core Principles\n8\t\n9\t1. **SQLite is the live store** — all mutations are SQL writes; reads are SQL queries. Fast, concurrent-read, serialized-write via WAL mode.\n10\t2. **JSONL is the git artifact** — exported on `bf sync`, committed to git, one entry per bead. Used for backup, cross-machine sharing, and recovery. Never written during normal operation.\n11\t3. **Drop-in CLI** — all `br` commands work under `bf` with the same flags and output formats\n12\t4. **`BEGIN IMMEDIATE` for atomic claim** — the read-score-update sequence runs inside a single SQLite write transaction, eliminating the race condition `br` has without requiring flock or a daemon\n13\t\n14\t---\n15\t\n16\t## Phase 1: Core Library — Data Model & JSONL Import/Export\n17\t\n18\t### 1.1 Data Model (`src/model.rs`)\n19\t\n20\tPort the exact `Issue`, `Status`, `Priority`, `IssueType`, `Dependency`, `DependencyType`, `Comment`, and `Event` structs from beads_rust with identical Serde attributes. This is the wire format — every field, every `skip_serializing_if`, every rename must match.\n21\t\n22\tKey structs and their JSONL serialization:\n23\t\n24\t```\n25\tStatus:       open | in_progress | blocked | deferred | draft | closed | tombstone | pinned | Custom(String)\n26\tPriority:     transparent i32 (0=Critical, 4=Backlog)\n27\tIssueType:    task | bug | feature | epic | chore | docs | question | Custom(String)\n28\tDependency:   { issue_id, depends_on_id, type (renamed from dep_type), created_at, created_by?, metadata?, thread_id? }\n29\tComment:      { id: i64, issue_id, author, text (renamed from body), created_at }\n30\tEvent:        { id: i64, issue_id, event_type, actor, old_value?, new_value?, comment?, created_at }\n31\t```\n32\t\n33\tIssue fields (alphabetical by JSON key):\n34\t```\n35\tid, title, description?, design?, acceptance_criteria?, notes?,\n36\tstatus, priority, issue_type, assignee?, owner?, estimated_minutes?,\n37\tcreated_at, created_by?, updated_at, closed_at?, close_reason?,\n38\tclosed_by_session?, due_at?, defer_until?, external_ref?,\n39\tsource_system?, source_repo, deleted_at?, deleted_by?, delete_reason?,\n40\toriginal_type?, compaction_level (default 0), compacted_at?,\n41\tcompacted_at_commit?, original_size?, sender?, ephemeral (default false),\n42\tpinned (default false), is_template (default false),\n43\tlabels: Vec<String>, dependencies: Vec<Dependency>, comments: Vec<Comment>\n44\t```\n45\t\n46\t### 1.2 JSONL Import (`src/jsonl.rs`)\n47\t\n48\tJSONL is read only during `bf sync --import` (pulling state from git) and `bf doctor --repair` (rebuilding SQLite from the artifact). Never read during normal CLI operation.\n49\t\n50\t```rust\n51\tfn import_jsonl(jsonl_path: &Path, storage: &Storage) -> Result<ImportResult> {\n52\t    let file = File::open(jsonl_path)?;\n53\t    let reader = BufReader::new(file);\n54\t    storage.with_write_transaction(|tx| {\n55\t        for line in reader.lines() {\n56\t            let issue: Issue = serde_json::from_str(&line?)?;\n57\t            tx.upsert_issue(&issue)?;\n58\t        }\n59\t        Ok(())\n60\t    })\n61\t}\n62\t```\n63\t\n64\tFunctions:\n65\t- `import_jsonl(path, storage)` — bulk upsert from JSONL into SQLite\n66\t- `stream_issues(path) -> impl Iterator<Item = Result<Issue>>` — lazy line iterator (used by import and doctor)\n67\t\n68\t### 1.3 JSONL Export (`src/jsonl.rs`)\n69\t\n70\tJSONL is written only during `bf sync --flush` (preparing the git artifact). Exports current bead state from SQLite, one entry per bead, sorted by ID for stable diffs. Atomic temp+rename.\n71\t\n72\t```rust\n73\tfn export_jsonl(jsonl_path: &Path, storage: &Storage) -> Result<ExportResult> {\n74\t    let issues = storage.list_all_issues()?;  // sorted by ID\n75\t    let temp_path = jsonl_path.with_extension(\"jsonl.tmp\");\n76\t    let mut writer = BufWriter::new(File::create_new(&temp_path)?);\n77\t    for issue in &issues {\n78\t        serde_json::to_writer(&mut writer, issue)?;\n79\t        writer.write_all(b\"\\n\")?;\n80\t    }\n81\t    writer.flush()?;\n82\t    drop(writer);\n83\t    fs::rename(&temp_path, jsonl_path)?;\n84\t    Ok(ExportResult { count: issues.len() })\n85\t}\n86\t```\n87\t\n88\tFunctions:\n89\t- `export_jsonl(path, storage)` — dump all beads from SQLite to JSONL (atomic)\n90\t- `export_jsonl_dirty(path, storage)` — export only dirty beads (incremental, faster for large workspaces)\n91\t\n92\t### 1.4 Config (`src/config.rs`)\n93\t\n94\tParse `.beads/config.yaml` with the same fields br uses:\n95\t\n96\t```yaml\n97\tissue_prefixes: [bd, fg]\n98\tdefault_priority: 2\n99\tdefault_type: task\n100\tscoring:\n101\t  priority_weight: 0.4\n102\t  blockers_weight: 0.3\n103\t  age_weight: 0.2\n104\t  labels_weight: 0.1\n105\t  max_age_hours: 20\n106\t  max_blockers: 3\n107\t# bead-forge additions (additive, br ignores these)\n108\tclaim_ttl_minutes: 30\n109\t```\n110\t\n111\tParse `.beads/metadata.json`:\n112\t```json\n113\t{ \"database\": \"beads.db\", \"jsonl_export\": \"issues.jsonl\" }\n114\t```\n115\t\n116\t### 1.5 ID Generation (`src/id.rs`)\n117\t\n118\tPort br's ID scheme: `<prefix>-<hash>` where hash is base36 lowercase. Use the birthday-problem adaptive length (3-8 chars). Read `issue_prefixes` from config (first entry is the default prefix).\n119\t\n120\t```rust\n121\tfn generate_id(prefix: &str, existing_count: usize) -> String {\n122\t    let len = optimal_hash_length(existing_count);\n123\t    let random_bytes = rand::random::<[u8; 16]>();\n124\t    let hash = sha256(&random_bytes);\n125\t    base36_encode(&hash[..len])\n126\t    format!(\"{}-{}\", prefix, hash)\n127\t}\n128\t```\n129\t\n130\t---\n131\t\n132\t## Phase 2: SQLite Primary Store\n133\t\n134\t### 2.1 Schema Application (`src/storage/schema.rs`)\n135\t\n136\tApply the exact same `CREATE TABLE IF NOT EXISTS` DDL from br's `SCHEMA_SQL`. Tables:\n137\t\n138\t| Table | Purpose |\n139\t|-------|---------|\n140\t| `issues` | All 35 columns, same types, defaults, CHECK constraints |\n141\t| `dependencies` | (issue_id, depends_on_id) PK, type, metadata, thread_id |\n142\t| `labels` | (issue_id, label) PK |\n143\t| `comments` | AUTOINCREMENT id, issue_id, author, text, created_at |\n144\t| `events` | AUTOINCREMENT id, issue_id, event_type, actor, old/new/comment |\n145\t| `config` | key-value |\n146\t| `metadata` | key-value |\n147\t| `dirty_issues` | Track which issues need JSONL export |\n148\t| `export_hashes` | Incremental export tracking |\n149\t| `blocked_issues_cache` | Materialized view of blocked issues |\n150\t| `child_counters` | Hierarchical IDs (bd-abc.1, bd-abc.2) |\n151\t| `recovery_sessions` | Anomaly/recovery audit trail |\n152\t| `anomaly_audit` | Recovery event tracking |\n153\t\n154\tAll indexes from br must be created identically, including the critical `idx_issues_ready` composite partial index.\n155\t\n156\t### 2.2 Storage Engine (`src/storage/sqlite.rs`)\n157\t\n158\tUse `rusqlite` (not FrankenSQLite) bundled with system SQLite. Apply WAL mode, foreign keys, busy_timeout=30s, cache_size=-8000, synchronous=NORMAL.\n159\t\n160\tAll mutations go through here. JSONL is never touched during normal operation.\n161\t\n162\tFunctions:\n163\t- `open(path: &Path) -> Result<Storage>` — open/create DB, apply schema\n164\t- `get_issue(id: &str) -> Result<Option<Issue>>` — point lookup by ID\n165\t- `list_issues(filter: IssueFilter) -> Result<Vec<Issue>>` — filtered query with WHERE clauses\n166\t- `list_all_issues() -> Result<Vec<Issue>>` — full table scan sorted by ID (for JSONL export)\n167\t- `create_issue(issue: &Issue) -> Result<()>` — INSERT\n168\t- `update_issue(id: &str, changes: IssueChanges) -> Result<()>` — UPDATE + mark dirty\n169\t- `close_issue(id: &str, reason: &str) -> Result<()>` — status transition + mark dirty\n170\t- `with_write_transaction(f) -> Result<T>` — execute closure in a write transaction\n171\t- `with_immediate_transaction(f) -> Result<T>` — `BEGIN IMMEDIATE` with retry (see §2.5) — acquires write lock before any reads (used by claim)\n172\t- `rebuild_blocked_cache() -> Result<()>` — recalculate blocked issues materialized view\n173\t\n174\t### 2.3 Sync Protocol (`src/sync.rs`)\n175\t\n176\tPort br's sync semantics:\n177\t\n178\t**Flush (SQLite → JSONL, for git)**:\n179\t1. Call `export_jsonl_dirty` — query dirty bead IDs, export full current state of each from SQLite\n180\t2. Atomic temp+rename over `issues.jsonl`\n181\t3. Clear `dirty_issues`, update `export_hashes`\n182\t\n183\tFor `bf sync` (full flush): call `export_jsonl` — dump all beads sorted by ID, unconditionally.\n184\t\n185\t**Import (JSONL → SQLite, from git pull)**:\n186\t1. Stream `issues.jsonl` line by line\n187\t2. Compare each with SQLite state using `content_hash`\n188\t3. INSERT new, UPDATE changed, SKIP unchanged\n189\t4. Handle collisions (same ID, different content) with deterministic resolution\n190\t\n191\t### 2.5 Concurrent Write Safety (`src/storage/sqlite.rs`)\n192\t\n193\tSQLite WAL mode serializes concurrent writers through a single write lock — they queue, not corrupt. `SQLITE_BUSY` is returned when a writer cannot acquire the lock within `busy_timeout`. With claim latency of ~1-2ms and a 20-worker fleet, the entire queue clears in ~20-40ms, so `SQLITE_BUSY` should never occur in normal operation. However, a retry wrapper is the cheap safety net that makes this a guarantee rather than an assumption:\n194\t\n195\t```rust\n196\tconst MAX_RETRIES: u32 = 5;\n197\tconst RETRY_BASE_MS: u64 = 50;\n198\t\n199\tfn with_immediate_transaction<T>(\n200\t    conn: &Connection,\n201\t    f: impl Fn(&Transaction) -> Result<T>,\n202\t) -> Result<T> {\n203\t    let mut attempt = 0;\n204\t    loop {\n205\t        match conn.execute(\"BEGIN IMMEDIATE\", []) {\n206\t            Ok(_) => {\n207\t                let tx = conn.unchecked_transaction()?;\n208\t                return match f(&tx) {\n209\t                    Ok(val) => { tx.commit()?; Ok(val) }\n210\t                    Err(e) => { let _ = tx.rollback(); Err(e) }\n211\t                };\n212\t            }\n213\t            Err(e) if is_busy_error(&e) && attempt < MAX_RETRIES => {\n214\t                attempt += 1;\n215\t                std::thread::sleep(Duration::from_millis(RETRY_BASE_MS * attempt as u64));\n216\t                continue;\n217\t            }\n218\t            Err(e) => return Err(e.into()),\n219\t        }\n220\t    }\n221\t}\n222\t\n223\tfn is_busy_error(e: &rusqlite::Error) -> bool {\n224\t    matches!(\n225\t        e,\n226\t        rusqlite::Error::SqliteFailure(\n227\t            rusqlite::ffi::Error { code: rusqlite::ErrorCode::DatabaseBusy, .. },\n228\t            _\n229\t        )\n230\t    )\n231\t}\n232\t```\n233\t\n234\t**Why this is sufficient and not a workaround**: `SQLITE_BUSY` with WAL mode is not data corruption — it is a clean \"lock unavailable, try again\" signal. The database is fully consistent when this occurs. The retry converts a transient contention spike (e.g., 20 workers all starting within the same millisecond) into a short wait rather than a user-visible error.\n235\t\n236\t**All write operations** (`claim`, `create`, `update`, `close`, `batch`) use `with_immediate_transaction`. Read-only operations (`list`, `show`, `ready`) use a plain `BEGIN DEFERRED` transaction and are never affected by write contention.\n237\t\n238\t### 2.7 Doctor/Repair (`src/doctor.rs`)\n239\t\n240\t- `doctor --repair`: Delete `beads.db`, reimport from JSONL\n241\t- `doctor --check`: Validate JSONL line integrity, check SQLite <-> JSONL consistency\n242\t- Recovery from corruption: JSONL export is always authoritative — `beads.db` can be rebuilt from it at any time\n243\t\n244\t---\n245\t\n246\t## Phase 3: CLI Commands\n247\t\n248\t### 3.1 Command Structure (`src/cli/`)\n249\t\n250\tUse `clap` with derive macros. Binary name: `bf`. Subcommands mirror br exactly.\n251\t\n252\t```\n253\tbf create    --title \"...\" --type <type> --priority <N> [--description \"...\"] [--label ...]\n254\tbf list      [--status <s>] [--type <t>] [--assignee <a>] [--limit N] [--format json|text|toon]\n255\tbf show      <id>\n256\tbf update    <id> [--status <s>] [--assignee <a>] [--priority <N>] [--title \"...\"] ...\n257\tbf close     <id> [--reason \"...\"]\n258\tbf reopen    <id>\n259\tbf delete    <id>\n260\tbf ready         [--limit N]                     # unblocked, open, sorted by priority\n261\tbf claim         --assignee <id>                 # atomic claim (see Phase 4)\n262\t                 [--model <model>]               # e.g. claude-sonnet-4-6\n263\t                 [--harness <name>]              # e.g. needle\n264\t                 [--harness-version <ver>]       # e.g. 0.5.2\n265\t                 [--workspace <path>] [--any]\n266\tbf critical-path <epic-id>                       # show critical path + float for each bead\n267\tbf dep           add-blocker <parent> <child>\n268\tbf dep           remove-blocker <parent> <child>\n269\tbf dep           tree <id>\n270\tbf label         <id> add <label>\n271\tbf label         <id> remove <label>\n272\tbf comment       <id> [--author <a>] [--text \"...\"]\n273\tbf sync          --flush-only\n274\tbf sync          --import-only\n275\tbf doctor        [--repair]\n276\tbf init          [--prefix <p>]\n277\tbf stats\n278\tbf count         [--status <s>]\n279\tbf search        <query>\n280\tbf schema\n281\tbf config        get <key>\n282\tbf config        set <key> <value>\n283\t```\n284\t\n285\t### 3.2 Output Formats\n286\t\n287\tThree formats, matching br exactly:\n288\t- **text**: Human-readable table (default for terminal)\n289\t- **json**: One JSON object per line (for piping)\n290\t- **toon**: Token-optimized output for LLM context windows\n291\t\n292\t### 3.3 Execution Model\n293\t\n294\tEach command:\n295\t1. Locate `.beads/` directory (walk up from CWD)\n296\t2. Load config + metadata\n297\t3. Open SQLite (`beads.db`), apply schema if new\n298\t4. Execute: mutations are SQL writes; reads are SQL queries\n299\t5. `bf sync` is the only command that touches `issues.jsonl` — flush exports it, import reads it\n300\t\n301\t---\n302\t\n303\t## Phase 4: Concurrent Claiming\n304\t\n305\t### 4.1 Architecture: SQLite `BEGIN IMMEDIATE`\n306\t\n307\tThe thundering herd problem — N workers racing to claim the same bead — is solved by running the entire read-score-update sequence inside a single `BEGIN IMMEDIATE` transaction. SQLite's write lock is acquired before any reads, so no two workers can read the same candidate state. No flock, no server, no daemon.\n308\t\n309\t```\n310\tWorker 1: BEGIN IMMEDIATE → SELECT candidates → score → UPDATE winner → COMMIT\n311\tWorker 2: BEGIN IMMEDIATE → (blocked at write lock until Worker 1 COMMITs) → SELECT → score → UPDATE → COMMIT\n312\tWorker 3: BEGIN IMMEDIATE → (blocked) → ...\n313\t...\n314\tWorker 20: BEGIN IMMEDIATE → (blocked) → SELECT → NONE (queue empty) → COMMIT (no-op)\n315\t```\n316\t\n317\tEach claim is a single CLI invocation. The critical section (lock held) is: SELECT scoring fields → score in memory → UPDATE winner + stale resets → COMMIT. Lock held for ~0.5-2ms.\n318\t\n319\t**Throughput**: SQLite handles claims purely in memory after the initial page cache warm-up:\n320\t\n321\t| Workspace | Active beads | Claim latency | Throughput |\n322\t|-----------|-------------|---------------|-----------|\n323\t| Typical (FORGE) | 248 | ~0.5ms | ~2000/sec |\n324\t| Medium (NEEDLE) | 518 | ~1ms | ~1000/sec |\n325\t| Large | 2000 | ~2ms | ~500/sec |\n326\t\n327\tWith 20 workers claiming simultaneously, the last worker waits ~20-40ms (19 queued transactions × ~1-2ms each). The fleet needs ~1-2 claims/sec at steady state — SQLite is overkill by 3 orders of magnitude.\n328\t\n329\t### 4.2 Atomic Claim (`src/claim.rs`)\n330\t\n331\tThe entire claim sequence runs inside a single `BEGIN IMMEDIATE` transaction. SQLite acquires the write lock before any reads, so no two workers can observe the same candidate state.\n332\t\n333\t```rust\n334\tfn claim(storage: &Storage, worker: &str, claim_ttl: Duration) -> Result<Option<Issue>> {\n335\t    storage.with_immediate_transaction(|tx| {\n336\t        let now = Utc::now();\n337\t\n338\t        // 1. Reclaim stale in_progress beads\n339\t        tx.execute(\n340\t            \"UPDATE issues SET status='open', assignee=NULL, updated_at=?1\n341\t             WHERE status='in_progress' AND updated_at < ?2\",\n342\t            params![now, now - claim_ttl],\n343\t        )?;\n344\t\n345\t        // 2. Load scoring fields for open, unblocked candidates\n346\t        //    (blocked_issues_cache is a materialized view maintained on dep changes)\n347\t        let candidates: Vec<ScoreEntry> = tx.query_map(\n348\t            \"SELECT id, priority, updated_at,\n349\t                    (SELECT COUNT(*) FROM dependencies d\n350\t                     JOIN issues b ON b.id = d.depends_on_id\n351\t                     WHERE d.issue_id IN (\n352\t                         SELECT issue_id FROM dependencies\n353\t                         WHERE depends_on_id = issues.id AND type='blocks'\n354\t                     ) AND b.status = 'open') AS downstream_impact\n355\t             FROM issues\n356\t             WHERE status = 'open'\n357\t               AND id NOT IN (SELECT issue_id FROM blocked_issues_cache)\n358\t             ORDER BY downstream_impact DESC, priority ASC, created_at ASC\",\n359\t            [],\n360\t            |row| ScoreEntry::from_row(row),\n361\t        )?;\n362\t\n363\t        if candidates.is_empty() {\n364\t            return Ok(None);\n365\t        }\n366\t\n367\t        // 3. Claim the top candidate\n368\t        let winner = &candidates[0];\n369\t        tx.execute(\n370\t            \"UPDATE issues SET status='in_progress', assignee=?1, updated_at=?2\n371\t             WHERE id=?3\",\n372\t            params![worker, now, winner.id],\n373\t        )?;\n374\t        tx.execute(\n375\t            \"INSERT INTO events (issue_id, event_type, actor, old_value, new_value, created_at)\n376\t             VALUES (?1, 'claimed', ?2, 'open', 'in_progress', ?3)\",\n377\t            params![winner.id, worker, now],\n378\t        )?;\n379\t        tx.mark_dirty(&winner.id)?;\n380\t\n381\t        Ok(Some(tx.get_issue(&winner.id)?))\n382\t    })\n383\t}\n384\t```\n385\t\n386\t**Key properties**:\n387\t- **Correctness**: `BEGIN IMMEDIATE` holds the SQLite write lock for the entire read-score-update sequence. No two workers can observe the same candidate state.\n388\t- **Crash safety**: If the process crashes mid-transaction, SQLite rolls back automatically. No partial state is committed.\n389\t- **Stale reclamation is a side effect**: The first statement in every claim resets expired `in_progress` beads before scoring. No separate process.\n390\t- **Impact-weighted scoring**: The query orders by `downstream_impact` (beads that would unblock the most work) then priority, then FIFO.\n391\t- **No flock, no file I/O**: The entire claim is in-memory SQL execution after page cache warm-up. `issues.jsonl` is not touched.\n392\t\n393\t### 4.3 Multi-Workspace Claiming (`src/claim.rs`)\n394\t\n395\tFor `bf claim --any` (claim from any workspace), open each workspace's SQLite, run the scoring query on each, pick the global winner, claim it:\n396\t\n397\t```rust\n398\tfn claim_any(workspace_paths: &[PathBuf], worker: &str, claim_ttl: Duration) -> Result<Option<Issue>> {\n399\t    // Score across all workspaces — each Storage::open is cheap (WAL, page cache)\n400\t    let mut best: Option<(Score, PathBuf)> = None;\n401\t    for path in workspace_paths {\n402\t        let storage = Storage::open(&path.join(\".beads/beads.db\"))?;\n403\t        if let Some(score) = storage.top_candidate_score(claim_ttl)? {\n404\t            if best.as_ref().map(|(b, _)| score > *b).unwrap_or(true) {\n405\t                best = Some((score, path.clone()));\n406\t            }\n407\t        }\n408\t    }\n409\t\n410\t    match best {\n411\t        None => Ok(None),\n412\t        Some((_, path)) => {\n413\t            let storage = Storage::open(&path.join(\".beads/beads.db\"))?;\n414\t            claim(&storage, worker, claim_ttl)\n415\t        }\n416\t    }\n417\t}\n418\t```\n419\t\n420\tNo cross-workspace locking needed — each `claim()` call uses `BEGIN IMMEDIATE` on its own SQLite file. Two workers racing on the same workspace are serialized by SQLite; two workers racing on different workspaces proceed in parallel.\n421\t\n422\t### 4.4 Stale Claim Detection\n423\t\n424\tNo background process needed. Stale detection runs as part of every `bf claim` invocation:\n425\t\n426\t1. Inside `BEGIN IMMEDIATE`: `UPDATE issues SET status='open' WHERE status='in_progress' AND updated_at < now - claim_ttl`\n427\t2. This runs before candidate scoring — stale beads become eligible again in the same transaction\n428\t3. Single SQL statement, no extra I/O\n429\t\n430\t**Claim TTL**: Default 30 minutes, configurable in `.beads/config.yaml`:\n431\t\n432\t```yaml\n433\tclaim_ttl_minutes: 30\n434\t```\n435\t\n436\t**TTL tuning**: With 20 workers and tasks taking 5-15 minutes, 30 minutes is conservative. A worker that's actively working but slow will have its bead remain `in_progress` — stale reclamation only triggers if the worker hasn't updated the bead in 30 minutes. Since the worker closes the bead when done (writing a new entry), active workers never get reclaimed.\n437\t\n438\t**Manual stale scan**: For workspaces with no active claiming (no fleet running), `bf doctor --reclaim-stale` performs the same scan without claiming a bead. Can be run via cron for long-running workspaces with occasional stuck claims.\n439\t\n440\t### 4.5 CLI Usage\n441\t\n442\t```bash\n443\t# Claim from current workspace\n444\tbf claim --assignee worker-7 --json\n445\t\n446\t# Claim with worker metadata (feeds velocity-aware scoring — see §4B.6)\n447\tbf claim --assignee worker-7 \\\n448\t         --model claude-sonnet-4-6 \\\n449\t         --harness needle \\\n450\t         --harness-version 0.5.2 \\\n451\t         --json\n452\t\n453\t# Claim from a specific workspace\n454\tbf claim --workspace containers/zai-proxy/ --assignee worker-3 --json\n455\t\n456\t# Claim highest priority across all workspaces\n457\tbf claim --any --assignee worker-12 --json\n458\t\n459\t# Prefer a workspace, fall back to any\n460\tbf claim --workspace containers/zai-proxy/ --fallback any --assignee worker-5 --json\n461\t```\n462\t\n463\tAll commands work identically in all modes — no server required, no daemon running. Each `bf claim` is a self-contained CLI invocation: lock, read, claim, write, unlock, exit.\n464\t\n465\tWorker metadata (`--model`, `--harness`, `--harness-version`) is stored in the claim event row and the `worker_sessions` table. It drives velocity-aware scoring (§4B.6) and appears in `bf log` output so you can see exactly which model/harness combination claimed each bead.\n466\t\n467\t### 4.6 Why No Server\n468\t\n469\tThe plan originally included a coordination server with `Arc<Mutex<ServerState>>`, in-memory priority queues, heartbeats, and a Unix socket protocol. This was removed because:\n470\t\n471\t1. **SQLite is sufficient**: `BEGIN IMMEDIATE` provides serialized write access. Claim latency is ~0.5-2ms — 4-16× faster than the previous flock+streaming-rewrite approach.\n472\t2. **Simpler operations**: No flock infrastructure, no streaming rewrite, no temp files during normal operation. All mutation logic is SQL.\n473\t3. **Crash recovery is automatic**: SQLite rolls back incomplete transactions on next open. No partial state, no temp file cleanup.\n474\t4. **Real-world scale validates it**: A 2,000-bead workspace takes ~2ms per claim. A 20-worker fleet needs ~1-2 claims/sec. SQLite delivers ~500 claims/sec at that size.\n475\t5. **Server is a future optimization**: A persistent in-memory server would reduce per-claim latency from ~2ms to ~0.1ms by eliminating SQLite file I/O entirely. Premature for current scale — can be added transparently later.\n476\t\n477\t### 4.7 Comparison to br's Race Condition\n478\t\n479\t| Scenario | br (beads_rust) | bf (bead-forge) |\n480\t|----------|-----------------|-----------------|\n481\t| 20 workers claim simultaneously | 20 read same JSONL, all see same \"next\" bead, all write `in_progress` — last writer wins, 19 workers have phantom claims | 20 workers serialized by SQLite write lock — each BEGIN IMMEDIATE sees post-commit state, each gets a distinct bead |\n482\t| Worker crashes mid-claim | N/A (no lock) | SQLite rolls back the incomplete transaction automatically on next open |\n483\t| Stale claim (worker died) | Bead stays `in_progress` forever | Next claim invocation reclaims beads older than TTL |\n484\t| Cross-workspace claiming | Not supported | `--any` locks all JSONL files in sorted order |\n485\t\n486\t---\n487\t\n488\t## Phase 4B: Extended Features\n489\t\n490\t### 4B.1 JSONL Rotation (`src/rotate.rs`)\n491\t\n492\tKeep `issues.jsonl` lean for fast claiming. With one entry per bead, the file grows only when new beads are created — but over a long project lifetime the accumulation of closed beads still grows the file. Rotation evicts closed beads into numbered archive files, keeping the active scan set small.\n493\t\n494\t```\n495\t.beads/\n496\t├── issues.jsonl          # active: open, in_progress, blocked, deferred + recently closed\n497\t├── issues.jsonl.1        # archive: closed beads rotated out most recently\n498\t├── issues.jsonl.2        # archive: older closed beads\n499\t└── issues.jsonl.3        # archive: oldest\n500\t```\n501\t\n502\t**Rotation rules**:\n503\t- `bf rotate` moves closed beads older than `rotate_age_days` (default 30) from `issues.jsonl` into `issues.jsonl.1` via streaming rewrite (active file) + streaming append (archive file)\n504\t- When `issues.jsonl.1` exceeds `rotate_max_size` (default 5MB), it becomes `issues.jsonl.2`, `.2` → `.3`, etc.\n505\t- Maximum archive files: `rotate_max_archives` (default 5). Oldest archive is deleted.\n506\t\n507\t**Claim only reads the active file**. This keeps claim latency proportional to the number of active (non-closed) beads rather than total workspace history.\n508\t\n509\t**Reading archived beads**: `bf show <id>` searches the active file first, then archives. `bf list --all` includes archives. `bf log <id>` searches all files for the full history.\n510\t\n511\t**git integration**: `.beads/issues.jsonl` is committed to git. Archive files (`.jsonl.1`, `.2`, ...) are also committed — they're part of the project history. The `.beads/` directory is the bead store and should be version-controlled alongside the code.\n512\t\n513\t**Secret protection**: Before any write, bf scans bead fields for secret patterns (AWS keys, private keys, API tokens, passwords) using a built-in regex set similar to git-secrets. If a match is found:\n514\t- `bf create` / `bf update` prints a warning and refuses the write\n515\t- `bf commit-check` (git pre-commit hook) scans staged changes to `.beads/` for secrets\n516\t- Patterns are configurable in `.beads/config.yaml`:\n517\t\n518\t```yaml\n519\tsecret_protection:\n520\t  enabled: true\n521\t  # Additional patterns (matched against all string fields)\n522\t  deny_patterns:\n523\t    - \"-----BEGIN (RSA |EC |DSA )?PRIVATE KEY-----\"\n524\t    - \"AKIA[0-9A-Z]{16}\"          # AWS access key\n525\t    - \"sk-[a-zA-Z0-9]{32,}\"       # OpenAI/Anthropic API key\n526\t  # Fields to exclude from scanning (e.g., known test values)\n527\t  allowlist_fields: []\n528\t```\n529\t\n530\tConfig:\n531\t\n532\t```yaml\n533\trotate_age_days: 30\n534\trotate_max_size_mb: 5\n535\trotate_max_archives: 5\n536\t```\n537\t\n538\t### 4B.2 Batch Operations (`src/batch.rs`)\n539\t\n540\tExecute multiple operations atomically under a single SQLite `BEGIN IMMEDIATE` transaction. Replaces sequences of N separate CLI invocations with one.\n541\t\n542\t```bash\n543\t# From a file\n544\tbf batch --file operations.json\n545\t\n546\t# From stdin (one operation per line)\n547\techo 'create --title \"child 1\" --type task\n548\tcreate --title \"child 2\" --type task\n549\tdep add-blocker fg-a3f8.1 fg-a3f8\n550\tdep add-blocker fg-a3f8.2 fg-a3f8\n551\tclose fg-a3f8 --reason \"Split into children\"' | bf batch\n552\t\n553\t# Programmatic JSON input\n554\tbf batch --json '[\n555\t  {\"op\": \"create\", \"title\": \"child 1\", \"type\": \"task\"},\n556\t  {\"op\": \"create\", \"title\": \"child 2\", \"type\": \"task\"},\n557\t  {\"op\": \"dep_add_blocker\", \"parent\": \"fg-a3f8.1\", \"child\": \"fg-a3f8\"},\n558\t  {\"op\": \"close\", \"id\": \"fg-a3f8\", \"reason\": \"Split\"}\n559\t]'\n560\t```\n561\t\n562\t**Atomicity**: All operations run inside a single SQLite write transaction (`BEGIN IMMEDIATE`). If any operation fails (invalid ID, bad status transition), the transaction rolls back — no partial state is committed.\n563\t\n564\t**Use cases**:\n565\t- NEEDLE mitosis: split 1 bead into N children (2N+1 operations → 1 batch)\n566\t- Bulk status changes: close all beads with a given label\n567\t- Migration: import beads from another tracker\n568\t- Workspace setup: create epics + child beads + dependencies in one shot\n569\t\n570\t**Output**: Returns JSON array of results, one per operation:\n571\t\n572\t```json\n573\t[\n574\t  {\"op\": 0, \"status\": \"ok\", \"id\": \"fg-b4d1\"},\n575\t  {\"op\": 1, \"status\": \"ok\", \"id\": \"fg-b4d2\"},\n576\t  {\"op\": 2, \"status\": \"ok\"},\n577\t  {\"op\": 3, \"status\": \"ok\"}\n578\t]\n579\t```\n580\t\n581\t### 4B.3 Annotations — Extensible Metadata (`src/model.rs`, `src/cli/annotate.rs`)\n582\t\n583\tArbitrary key-value pairs on any bead, stored as `annotations: BTreeMap<String, String>`. External tools (NEEDLE, custom scripts) can store structured metadata without modifying bf's schema.\n584\t\n585\t```bash\n586\t# Set annotations\n587\tbf annotate fg-a3f8 needle_attempt=3 needle_session=abc123\n588\tbf annotate fg-a3f8 review_status=needs_review\n589\t\n590\t# Remove annotations\n591\tbf annotate fg-a3f8 --remove needle_error\n592\t\n593\t# Query by annotation\n594\tbf list --annotation needle_attempt=3\n595\tbf list --annotation review_status=needs_review\n596\t\n597\t# Show annotations (included in bf show output)\n598\tbf show fg-a3f8 --json | jq '.annotations'\n599\t```\n600\t\n601\t**Data model change**: Add to Issue struct:\n602\t\n603\t```rust\n604\t#[serde(default, skip_serializing_if = \"BTreeMap::is_empty\")]\n605\tpub annotations: BTreeMap<String, String>,\n606\t```\n607\t\n608\tThis is additive — br ignores unknown fields, so backward compatibility is maintained.\n609\t\n610\t**Use cases**:\n611\t- NEEDLE: `needle_attempt`, `needle_session`, `needle_error`, `needle_worker_version`\n612\t- Custom tools: `ci_build_id`, `deployment_sha`, `jira_key`\n613\t- Fleet tracking: `claimed_at`, `heartbeat_at`, `estimated_minutes_remaining`\n614\t\n615\t### 4B.4 Operation History — `bf log` (`src/log.rs`)\n616\t\n617\tShow the history of mutations on a specific bead or workspace, sourced from the SQLite events table and git history.\n618\t\n619\t```bash\n620\tbf log fg-a3f8                          # full history of this bead\n621\tbf log --since \"2026-04-25\"             # all workspace changes since date\n622\tbf log --actor worker-3                 # changes by a specific worker\n623\tbf log --limit 20                       # last 20 mutations\n624\tbf log --status-changes                 # only status transitions\n625\t```\n626\t\n627\tOutput:\n628\t\n629\t```\n630\t2026-04-25 10:00  CREATED     by: human        \"Implement auth flow\"\n631\t2026-04-25 10:05  DEP_ADD     by: human        blocked by fg-b2c1\n632\t2026-04-25 14:30  CLAIMED     by: worker-3     status: open → in_progress\n633\t2026-04-25 15:45  COMMENT     by: worker-3     \"Found edge case in token refresh\"\n634\t2026-04-25 16:00  CLOSED      by: worker-3     \"Completed\"\n635\t```\n636\t\n637\t**Implementation**: History is sourced from two places:\n638\t\n639\t1. **SQLite events table** (primary): every mutation records an event row (`event_type`, `actor`, `old_value`, `new_value`). `bf log` queries this table directly — O(1) lookup by issue ID, no file scanning.\n640\t\n641\t2. **Git history** (fallback/deep history): `issues.jsonl` is committed to git on each sync. `git log -p .beads/issues.jsonl` shows every past state of the file. `bf log --git` uses this for history older than the events table retention window.\n642\t\n643\tSince JSONL has one entry per bead (not a mutation log), JSONL diffing is not used for history. The events table is the authoritative mutation record.\n644\t\n645\t**`bf log --diff`**: Show the field-level diff from the events table:\n646\t\n647\t```bash\n648\tbf log fg-a3f8 --diff\n649\t# 2026-04-25 14:30  CLAIMED\n650\t#   - status: \"open\" → \"in_progress\"\n651\t#   + assignee: null → \"worker-3\"\n652\t#   + annotations.needle_attempt: \"1\" → \"2\"\n653\t```\n654\t\n655\t### 4B.5 Critical Path Computation (`src/critical_path.rs`)\n656\t\n657\tComputes the longest dependency chain through the workspace graph and annotates each bead with its **float** — how many hops it can slip before delaying the epic. Beads with `float == 0` are on the critical path; every day they're blocked delays completion by a day.\n658\t\n659\t**Command**:\n660\t\n661\t```bash\n662\t$ bf critical-path fg-epic-auth\n663\t\n664\tCritical path for fg-epic-auth (14 open beads, 3 on critical path):\n665\t\n666\t  float=0  [fg-a3f8] Implement auth token refresh        in_progress (worker-3)\n667\t  float=0  [fg-b2c1] Fix concurrent session state bug    open\n668\t  float=0  [fg-c4d9] Integration tests: auth flow        open\n669\t  float=2  [fg-d5e3] Update API documentation            open\n670\t  float=2  [fg-e6f4] Refactor error response format      open\n671\t  float=5  [fg-f7g5] Add rate limiting headers           open\n672\t  ...\n673\t\n674\tLongest chain: fg-a3f8 → fg-b2c1 → fg-c4d9 → [epic closes]\n675\tMinimum remaining time: 3 bead-completions on critical path\n676\t```\n677\t\n678\t**Algorithm**: Two-pass walk on the dependency DAG using SQLite recursive CTEs.\n679\t\n680\tPass 1 (forward — compute earliest start `ES`): start from beads with no open predecessors (`ES=0`). For each bead, `ES = max(ES of all open predecessors) + 1`.\n681\t\n682\tPass 2 (backward — compute latest start `LS`): start from the epic. For each bead, `LS = min(LS of all successors) - 1`. `float = LS - ES`. Zero-float beads form the critical path.\n683\t\n684\t```sql\n685\tWITH RECURSIVE\n686\t  -- Forward pass: earliest start for each open bead\n687\t  forward(id, es) AS (\n688\t    SELECT i.id, 0\n689\t    FROM issues i\n690\t    WHERE i.status IN ('open', 'in_progress')\n691\t      AND NOT EXISTS (\n692\t        SELECT 1 FROM dependencies d\n693\t        JOIN issues pred ON pred.id = d.depends_on_id\n694\t        WHERE d.issue_id = i.id AND d.type = 'blocks'\n695\t          AND pred.status IN ('open', 'in_progress')\n696\t      )\n697\t    UNION ALL\n698\t    SELECT d.issue_id, MAX(f.es) + 1\n699\t    FROM dependencies d\n700\t    JOIN forward f ON f.id = d.depends_on_id\n701\t    WHERE d.type = 'blocks'\n702\t    GROUP BY d.issue_id\n703\t  )\n704\tSELECT id, es,\n705\t       (SELECT MAX(es) FROM forward) - es AS float\n706\tFROM forward\n707\tORDER BY float ASC, es ASC;\n708\t```\n709\t\n710\t**Schema addition**: `critical_path_cache` table — recomputed whenever a dependency is added/removed or a bead changes status. Invalidated by a trigger on `dependencies` and `issues.status`.\n711\t\n712\t```sql\n713\tCREATE TABLE critical_path_cache (\n714\t    bead_id     TEXT PRIMARY KEY REFERENCES issues(id),\n715\t    epic_id     TEXT REFERENCES issues(id),\n716\t    es          INTEGER NOT NULL,   -- earliest start (hops from root)\n717\t    ls          INTEGER NOT NULL,   -- latest start\n718\t    float       INTEGER NOT NULL,   -- ls - es; 0 = critical path\n719\t    updated_at  DATETIME NOT NULL\n720\t);\n721\t```\n722\t\n723\t**Integration with claim scoring**: The claim query joins `critical_path_cache` and adds a large bonus for zero-float beads:\n724\t\n725\t```sql\n726\t1000.0 / (COALESCE(cp.float, 999) + 1) AS critical_path_bonus\n727\t```\n728\t\n729\tA zero-float bead gets `1000 / 1 = 1000` bonus. A float-5 bead gets `1000 / 6 ≈ 167`. A bead not on any epic path gets `1000 / 1000 = 1`. This ensures critical-path beads always sort above non-critical beads regardless of their listed priority.\n730\t\n731\t**`bf dep add-blocker` side effect**: Every time a dependency is created or removed, the cache for the affected epic is invalidated and recomputed inside the same `BEGIN IMMEDIATE` transaction. Recompute cost is O(V + E) — for a 500-bead workspace with 300 deps, under 1ms.\n732\t\n733\t### 4B.6 Velocity-Aware Impact Scoring (`src/velocity.rs`)\n734\t\n735\tThe claim scorer currently orders by `downstream_impact / priority`. That's correct for maximizing throughput when all workers and task types take similar time. In practice, a `claude-opus-4-7` worker closes `bug` beads in 8 minutes while the same harness on `claude-haiku-4-5` takes 35 minutes for the same type — a 4× difference. The optimal claim for each worker is the task where `impact / expected_duration` is maximized for *that specific worker configuration*, not the global impact rank.\n736\t\n737\t**Worker metadata on claim**: Workers pass their composition to `bf claim`:\n738\t\n739\t```bash\n740\tbf claim --assignee worker-01 \\\n741\t         --model claude-sonnet-4-6 \\\n742\t         --harness needle \\\n743\t         --harness-version 0.5.2 \\\n744\t         --json\n745\t```\n746\t\n747\t**Schema**:\n748\t\n749\t```sql\n750\t-- One row per worker session (created on bf claim, updated on bf close)\n751\tCREATE TABLE worker_sessions (\n752\t    session_id      TEXT PRIMARY KEY,  -- UUID generated by worker\n753\t    worker_id       TEXT NOT NULL,\n754\t    model           TEXT,              -- 'claude-sonnet-4-6', 'claude-opus-4-7', etc.\n755\t    harness         TEXT,              -- 'needle', 'custom'\n756\t    harness_version TEXT,              -- '0.5.2'\n757\t    bead_id         TEXT REFERENCES issues(id),\n758\t    claimed_at      DATETIME,\n759\t    closed_at       DATETIME,\n760\t    duration_seconds INTEGER           -- populated on bf close\n761\t);\n762\t\n763\t-- Aggregated velocity statistics per (model, harness, issue_type)\n764\tCREATE TABLE velocity_stats (\n765\t    model           TEXT NOT NULL,\n766\t    harness         TEXT NOT NULL,\n767\t    issue_type      TEXT NOT NULL,\n768\t    sample_count    INTEGER DEFAULT 0,\n769\t    p50_seconds     INTEGER,\n770\t    p90_seconds     INTEGER,\n771\t    avg_seconds     REAL,\n772\t    last_updated    DATETIME,\n773\t    PRIMARY KEY (model, harness, issue_type)\n774\t);\n775\t```\n776\t\n777\t**Update on close**: When `bf close <id>` is called, if the closing worker passed `--session-id <uuid>`, the session row is updated with `closed_at` and `duration_seconds`. A trigger recomputes `velocity_stats` for that `(model, harness, issue_type)` tuple using a window over the last 50 sessions.\n778\t\n779\t**Claim scoring integration**: The claim query joins `velocity_stats` for the requesting worker and computes `score = impact / expected_seconds`:\n780\t\n781\t```sql\n782\tSELECT\n783\t    i.id,\n784\t    i.priority,\n785\t    i.issue_type,\n786\t    COALESCE(cp.float, 999)            AS critical_float,\n787\t    COALESCE(vs.p50_seconds, 1800)     AS expected_seconds,\n788\t    -- Combined score: more impact per unit time = higher priority\n789\t    (\n790\t      downstream_impact * 3.0\n791\t      + (4 - i.priority) * 2.0\n792\t      + 1000.0 / (COALESCE(cp.float, 999) + 1)\n793\t    ) / COALESCE(vs.p50_seconds, 1800) AS score\n794\tFROM issues i\n795\tLEFT JOIN critical_path_cache cp  ON cp.bead_id = i.id\n796\tLEFT JOIN velocity_stats vs       ON vs.issue_type = i.issue_type\n797\t                                 AND vs.model    = ?model\n798\t                                 AND vs.harness  = ?harness\n799\tWHERE i.status = 'open'\n800\t  AND i.id NOT IN (SELECT issue_id FROM blocked_issues_cache)\n801\tORDER BY score DESC\n802\tLIMIT 1\n803\t```\n804\t\n805\tWorkers with no velocity history use the 1800s (30-minute) default — conservative but correct. After ~10 completions per type, the estimate is meaningful.\n806\t\n807\t**`bf velocity` command**: Show the velocity table for all known worker configurations:\n808\t\n809\t```\n810\t$ bf velocity\n811\t\n812\tModel                  Harness   Type     Samples  p50    p90\n813\tclaude-opus-4-7        needle    task     142      8m     22m\n814\tclaude-opus-4-7        needle    bug      38       14m    51m\n815\tclaude-sonnet-4-6      needle    task     87       18m    45m\n816\tclaude-sonnet-4-6      needle    bug      24       31m    1h12m\n817\tclaude-haiku-4-5       needle    task     23       35m    2h10m\n818\t```\n819\t\n820\tThis table surfaces which model+harness combinations are most efficient for which task types — direct input for fleet composition decisions (which models to provision for which workspace).\n821\t\n822\t**Fallback**: If `--model` is not passed to `bf claim`, the scorer uses the average across all models for that issue type. Backward compatible — undecorated `bf claim` calls work exactly as before, just without per-model scoring.\n823\t\n824\t---\n825\t\n826\t## Phase 5: NEEDLE Integration\n827\t\n828\tNEEDLE's `bead_store/mod.rs` chains several `br` CLI calls that have race windows between them. Each race is eliminated by the corresponding `bf` command.\n829\t\n830\t### 5.1 Race 1 — `claim()`: two-process verify (lines 518-558)\n831\t\n832\t**br (racy)**:\n833\t```rust\n834\t// Call 1: br update <id> --status in_progress --assignee <actor>\n835\t// ← race window: another worker sees this bead as open and claims it ←\n836\t// Call 2: br show <id>  (to verify .assignee == actor)\n837\t```\n838\tTwo processes, two SQLite opens. If two workers race, both issue `br update` and `br` does not enforce exclusivity — it just overwrites. The `br show` verify is too late: the wrong worker may have overwritten the `assignee` field between the two calls.\n839\t\n840\t**bf (atomic)**:\n841\t```bash\n842\tbead=$(bf claim --workspace \"$WORKSPACE\" --assignee \"$WORKER\" --json)\n843\t```\n844\t`bf claim` runs the full read-score-update sequence inside a single `BEGIN IMMEDIATE` transaction. No second call, no verify step needed.\n845\t\n846\t### 5.2 Race 2 — `ready()` → `claim()`: TOCTOU (lines 487-507)\n847\t\n848\t**br (racy)**:\n849\t```rust\n850\t// Call 1: br ready --json  → returns candidate list (a snapshot)\n851\t// ← race window: another worker claims the top candidate ←\n852\t// Call 2: claim(selected_id)  → may be claiming an already-claimed bead\n853\t```\n854\tThe winning bead is selected from a stale snapshot. By the time `claim()` issues `br update`, the bead may have been claimed by another worker.\n855\t\n856\t**bf (atomic)**:\n857\t```bash\n858\tbead=$(bf claim --workspace \"$WORKSPACE\" --assignee \"$WORKER\" --json)\n859\t```\n860\tScoring and claiming happen inside the same `BEGIN IMMEDIATE` transaction. The candidate list is read and the winner is updated atomically — no snapshot staleness.\n861\t\n862\t### 5.3 Race 3 — Mitosis: `create_bead` + `add_dependency` (lines 607-639)\n863\t\n864\t**br (non-atomic)**:\n865\t```rust\n866\t// Call 1: br create \"child title\"  → returns new bead ID\n867\t// ← process crash here → orphaned bead with no dependency link ←\n868\t// Call 2: br dep add <parent_id> <child_id>\n869\t```\n870\tIf NEEDLE dies between `br create` and `br dep add`, the child bead exists but is not linked to the parent. The parent is never closed; the orphaned child is never picked up.\n871\t\n872\t**bf (atomic)**:\n873\t```bash\n874\tbf batch --json '[\n875\t  {\"op\": \"create\", \"title\": \"child 1\", \"type\": \"task\"},\n876\t  {\"op\": \"create\", \"title\": \"child 2\", \"type\": \"task\"},\n877\t  {\"op\": \"dep_add_blocker\", \"parent\": \"fg-a3f8.1\", \"child\": \"fg-a3f8\"},\n878\t  {\"op\": \"dep_add_blocker\", \"parent\": \"fg-a3f8.2\", \"child\": \"fg-a3f8\"},\n879\t  {\"op\": \"close\", \"id\": \"fg-a3f8\", \"reason\": \"Split into children\"}\n880\t]'\n881\t```\n882\tAll five operations run inside one `BEGIN IMMEDIATE` transaction. If NEEDLE dies mid-batch, the transaction rolls back automatically — no partial state.\n883\t\n884\t### 5.4 Inefficiency — `labels()` round-trip (lines 584-588)\n885\t\n886\t**br (wasteful)**:\n887\t```rust\n888\tasync fn labels(&self, id: &BeadId) -> Result<Vec<String>> {\n889\t    let bead = self.show(id).await?;  // full br show just to get .labels\n890\t    Ok(bead.labels)\n891\t}\n892\t```\n893\tOne full `br show` (with JSON deserialization of all 35 fields) to extract one field.\n894\t\n895\t**bf (direct)**:\n896\t```bash\n897\tbf labels <id> --json   # SELECT label FROM labels WHERE issue_id = ?\n898\t```\n899\tDirect `SELECT` on the `labels` table. Single column, single round-trip.\n900\t\n901\t### 5.5 Inefficiency — Multiple `br label add` calls\n902\t\n903\t**br (unbatched)**:\n904\t```rust\n905\tfor label in &labels {\n906\t    br_label_add(id, label).await?;   // separate process per label\n907\t}\n908\t```\n909\tN labels = N process invocations = N SQLite open/close cycles.\n910\t\n911\t**bf (batched)**:\n912\t```bash\n913\tbf label <id> add label1 label2 label3   # one INSERT per label, one transaction\n914\t```\n915\t\n916\t### 5.6 Pluck Strand Update\n917\t\n918\tOne-line change in NEEDLE's `pluck.sh` or `bead_store/mod.rs`:\n919\t\n920\t```bash\n921\t# Old (racy — two br calls with a race window between them):\n922\t# br ready --json | pick_top | xargs br update --status in_progress --assignee \"$WORKER\"\n923\t\n924\t# New (atomic — single bf call, BEGIN IMMEDIATE claim):\n925\tbead=$(bf claim --workspace \"$WORKSPACE\" --assignee \"$WORKER\" --json)\n926\t```\n927\t\n928\t### 5.7 Close/Block Remains Same\n929\t\n930\t```bash\n931\tbf close \"$bead_id\" --reason \"Completed: ...\"\n932\tbf update \"$bead_id\" --status blocked\n933\t```\n934\t\n935\tThese are single-operation writes with no race condition — no change needed.\n936\t\n937\t### 5.8 Symlink for Backward Compatibility\n938\t\n939\t```bash\n940\tln -sf ~/.local/bin/bf ~/.local/bin/br\n941\t```\n942\t\n943\tAll existing scripts using `br` commands work without modification. NEEDLE's non-atomic chains are replaced incrementally — `bf claim` and `bf batch` are the high-priority fixes; the rest can migrate when convenient.\n944\t\n945\t---\n946\t\n947\t## Phase 6: Build & Deploy\n948\t\n949\t### 6.1 Project Structure\n950\t\n951\t```\n952\tbead-forge/\n953\t├── Cargo.toml\n954\t├── src/\n955\t│   ├── main.rs              # CLI entry point\n956\t│   ├── lib.rs               # Library root\n957\t│   ├── model.rs             # Issue, Status, Priority, Annotations\n958\t│   ├── jsonl.rs             # JSONL import (sync --import) + export (sync --flush)\n959\t│   ├── config.rs            # Config + Metadata parsing\n960\t│   ├── id.rs                # ID generation\n961\t│   ├── claim.rs             # Atomic BEGIN IMMEDIATE claiming + impact scoring\n962\t│   ├── rotate.rs            # JSONL log rotation\n963\t│   ├── batch.rs             # Batch operations under single BEGIN IMMEDIATE transaction\n964\t│   ├── log.rs               # Operation history from JSONL event log\n965\t│   ├── secrets.rs           # Secret pattern scanning\n966\t│   ├── cli/\n967\t│   │   ├── mod.rs           # clap app definition\n968\t│   │   ├── create.rs\n969\t│   │   ├── list.rs\n970\t│   │   ├── show.rs\n971\t│   │   ├── update.rs\n972\t│   │   ├── close.rs\n973\t│   │   ├── reopen.rs\n974\t│   │   ├── delete.rs\n975\t│   │   ├── ready.rs\n976\t│   │   ├── claim.rs         # `bf claim` subcommand\n977\t│   │   ├── annotate.rs      # `bf annotate` subcommand\n978\t│   │   ├── batch.rs         # `bf batch` subcommand\n979\t│   │   ├── log.rs           # `bf log` subcommand\n980\t│   │   ├── rotate.rs        # `bf rotate` subcommand\n981\t│   │   ├── dep.rs\n982\t│   │   ├── label.rs\n983\t│   │   ├── comment.rs\n984\t│   │   ├── sync.rs\n985\t│   │   ├── doctor.rs\n986\t│   │   ├── init.rs\n987\t│   │   ├── search.rs\n988\t│   │   └── stats.rs\n989\t│   ├── storage/\n990\t│   │   ├── mod.rs\n991\t│   │   ├── schema.rs        # SQLite DDL (identical to br)\n992\t│   │   └── sqlite.rs        # rusqlite storage backend\n993\t│   └── format/\n994\t│       ├── mod.rs\n995\t│       ├── text.rs\n996\t│       ├── json.rs\n997\t│       └── toon.rs\n998\t├── tests/\n999\t│   ├── jsonl_compat.rs      # Round-trip tests with br JSONL files\n1000\t│   ├── schema_compat.rs     # Verify SQLite schema matches br\n1001\t│   ├── claim_race.rs        # Concurrent BEGIN IMMEDIATE claim tests\n1002\t│   ├── batch_atomic.rs      # Batch rollback on failure\n1003\t│   └── secret_scanning.rs   # Secret pattern detection\n1004\t└── build.rs\n1005\t```\n1006\t\n1007\t### 6.2 Dependencies\n1008\t\n1009\t```toml\n1010\t[dependencies]\n1011\tclap = { version = \"4\", features = [\"derive\"] }\n1012\tserde = { version = \"1\", features = [\"derive\"] }\n1013\tserde_json = \"1\"\n1014\tserde_yaml = \"0.9\"\n1015\tchrono = { version = \"0.4\", features = [\"serde\"] }\n1016\trusqlite = { version = \"0.31\", features = [\"bundled\"] }\n1017\tsha2 = \"0.10\"\n1018\trand = \"0.8\"\n1019\tregex = \"1\"                 # Secret pattern scanning\n1020\ttracing = \"0.1\"\n1021\ttracing-subscriber = \"0.3\"\n1022\tanyhow = \"1\"\n1023\tthiserror = \"1\"\n1024\t```\n1025\t\n1026\t### 6.3 CI via Argo Workflows\n1027\t\n1028\tAdd a `bead-forge-build` WorkflowTemplate to `jedarden/declarative-config`. Builds the Rust binary in a container, pushes to `ronaldraygun/bead-forge`.\n1029\t\n1030\t### 6.4 Deployment\n1031\t\n1032\tDeploy as a standalone binary to the Hetzner server at `~/.local/bin/bf`. Symlink `br` -> `bf` for backward compatibility. No daemon, no systemd unit — each `bf` invocation is self-contained.\n1033\t\n1034\t---\n1035\t\n1036\t## Compatibility Verification\n1037\t\n1038\t### JSONL Round-Trip Test\n1039\t\n1040\tEvery release must pass this test:\n1041\t\n1042\t```bash\n1043\t# 1. Take a real br workspace\n1044\tcp -r /home/coding/FORGE/.beads /tmp/test-beads\n1045\t\n1046\t# 2. bf reads the JSONL\n1047\tbf list --format json > /tmp/bf-output.jsonl\n1048\t\n1049\t# 3. br reads the same JSONL\n1050\tcd /home/coding/FORGE && br list --format json > /tmp/br-output.jsonl\n1051\t\n1052\t# 4. Compare (order-independent by ID)\n1053\tdiff <(jq -S . /tmp/bf-output.jsonl) <(jq -S . /tmp/br-output.jsonl)\n1054\t# Must be identical\n1055\t```\n1056\t\n1057\t### SQLite Compatibility Test\n1058\t\n1059\t```bash\n1060\t# 1. bf creates/updates beads in a workspace\n1061\tbf create --title \"compat test\" --type task\n1062\tbf list\n1063\t\n1064\t# 2. br reads the same workspace\n1065\tbr list\n1066\tbr doctor\n1067\t# Must succeed with no errors\n1068\t```\n1069\t\n1070\t### Claim Race Test\n1071\t\n1072\t```bash\n1073\t# Setup: create a test workspace with 10 beads of varying priority\n1074\tcd /tmp && rm -rf bf-test && mkdir bf-test && cd bf-test && bf init --prefix bf\n1075\tfor i in $(seq 1 10); do\n1076\t  bf create --title \"test-$i\" --priority $((i % 5))\n1077\tdone\n1078\t\n1079\t# === Test 1: Basic thundering herd (20 workers, 10 beads) ===\n1080\t# 20 workers claim simultaneously. Exactly 10 get a bead, 10 get NONE.\n1081\tfor i in $(seq 1 20); do\n1082\t  bf claim --any --assignee \"worker-$i\" --json > /tmp/claim-$i.out 2>&1 &\n1083\tdone\n1084\twait\n1085\t\n1086\t# Verify: exactly 10 claims succeeded, 10 returned NONE\n1087\tgrep -cl '\"id\"' /tmp/claim-*.out | wc -l  # must be 10\n1088\tgrep -cl 'NONE' /tmp/claim-*.out | wc -l  # must be 10\n1089\t\n1090\t# Verify: no bead claimed by more than one worker\n1091\tcat /tmp/claim-*.out | jq -r '.id' | sort | uniq -c | sort -rn\n1092\t# Every ID must appear exactly once\n1093\t\n1094\t# === Test 2: Priority ordering ===\n1095\t# The 10 workers that succeeded should have beads in priority order\n1096\t# (priority 0 beads claimed before priority 4)\n1097\t# Verify by correlating claim output order with priority values\n1098\t\n1099\t# === Test 3: Sequential claims (depletion) ===\n1100\t# Create 20 more beads, claim one at a time, verify queue drains\n1101\tfor i in $(seq 11 30); do\n1102\t  bf create --title \"test-$i\" --priority $((i % 5))\n1103\tdone\n1104\tfor i in $(seq 1 20); do\n1105\t  result=$(bf claim --any --assignee \"seq-worker-$i\" --json)\n1106\t  [ -n \"$result\" ] && echo \"$result\" | jq -r '.id'\n1107\tdone\n1108\tbf list --status open --format json\n1109\t# Must return empty — all beads claimed\n1110\t\n1111\t# === Test 4: Stale claim reclamation ===\n1112\t# Claim a bead, manually age its updated_at past claim_ttl\n1113\t# Then claim again — the stale bead should be reclaimed and re-claimable\n1114\tbf claim --any --assignee \"dead-worker\" --json\n1115\t# (test harness: set claim_ttl to 5s for this test, or mock updated_at)\n1116\tbf doctor --reclaim-stale --ttl 0s\n1117\tbf list --status open --format json\n1118\t# The dead-worker's bead must be back in open status\n1119\t\n1120\t# === Test 5: Stale reclamation as side effect ===\n1121\t# Dead worker's bead is reclaimed when another worker claims\n1122\tbf claim --any --assignee \"scavenger\" --json\n1123\t# scavenger gets a bead; dead-worker's bead is also reclaimed to open\n1124\t\n1125\t# === Test 6: Multi-workspace claiming ===\n1126\t# Create two workspaces, claim --any gets highest priority across both\n1127\tmkdir /tmp/ws-a && cd /tmp/ws-a && bf init --prefix wa\n1128\tmkdir /tmp/ws-b && cd /tmp/ws-b && bf init --prefix wb\n1129\tbf create --title \"ws-a high\" --priority 0   # in ws-b\n1130\tbf create --title \"ws-a low\"  --priority 4   # in ws-b\n1131\tcd /tmp/ws-a && bf create --title \"ws-a mid\" --priority 2\n1132\tbf claim --any --assignee \"multi-worker\" --json --workspace /tmp/ws-a --workspace /tmp/ws-b\n1133\t# Should get ws-b's \"ws-a high\" (priority 0)\n1134\t```\n1135\t\n1136\t---\n1137\t\n1138\t## Implementation Order\n1139\t\n1140\t| Phase | Description | Estimated Effort |\n1141\t|-------|-------------|-----------------|\n1142\t| 1 | Core library (model, JSONL read/write, config, ID gen) | Foundation |\n1143\t| 2 | SQLite cache layer (schema, storage, sync, doctor) | Medium |\n1144\t| 3 | CLI commands (all br-compatible commands) | Medium |\n1145\t| 4 | Concurrent claiming (BEGIN IMMEDIATE, impact scoring, stale reclamation, multi-workspace) | Medium |\n1146\t| 4B | Extended features (log rotation, batch ops, annotations, operation history, secret scanning, critical path, velocity scoring) | Medium |\n1147\t| 5 | NEEDLE integration (pluck.sh update, backward compat) | Small |\n1148\t| 6 | Build & deploy (CI, binary) | Small |\n1149\t\n1150\tPhases 1-3 produce a fully functional standalone `bf` that replaces `br`. Phase 4 adds atomic claiming for fleet operations. Phase 4B adds extended features that make bf more powerful than br. Phases 5-6 integrate and deploy.\n1151\t\n1152\t---\n1153\t\n1154\t## Key Design Decisions\n1155\t\n1156\t1. **SQLite-primary, JSONL as git artifact**: SQLite is the live database — all reads and writes go through it. JSONL is exported on `bf sync` for git commit, providing backup, cross-machine sharing, and recovery. This matches how bd and br work, but with rusqlite (no corruption) and `BEGIN IMMEDIATE` for atomic claim (no race condition).\n1157\t\n1158\t2. **rusqlite, not FrankenSQLite**: We already proved in the beads_rust fork that FrankenSQLite has corruption issues. Start clean with rusqlite.\n1159\t\n1160\t3. **`BEGIN IMMEDIATE` for atomic claim**: The read-score-update sequence runs in a single SQLite write transaction. No flock, no streaming rewrite, no temp files. SQLite's own locking serializes concurrent claims correctly.\n1161\t\n1162\t4. **No automatic git commits**: Match br's explicit, non-invasive philosophy. Users run `bf sync` when they want to commit JSONL changes.\n1163\t\n1164\t5. **Cattle, not pets**: Workers are disposable fleet units with no identity, no memory, and no conversation. Claims are atomic SQL dequeues from a priority queue, not negotiations.\n1165\t\n1166\t6. **Stale reclamation as a side effect of claiming**: The first statement in every `BEGIN IMMEDIATE` claim transaction resets expired `in_progress` beads. No separate heartbeat system, no background process.\n1167\t\n1168\t7. **Server as future optimization, not v1**: A persistent in-memory server would reduce per-claim latency from ~2ms to ~0.1ms by eliminating SQLite file I/O. Premature for current scale — can be added transparently later.\n1169\t\n1170\t8. **Rotation keeps JSONL artifact lean**: Closed beads older than `rotate_age_days` are exported to archive files (`issues.jsonl.1`, etc.) rather than the active `issues.jsonl`. Keeps the committed artifact small and git diffs readable.\n1171\t\n1172\t9. **Annotations as extension mechanism**: Arbitrary `BTreeMap<String, String>` on beads lets external tools (NEEDLE, custom scripts) store structured metadata without schema changes. br ignores unknown fields, so backward compatibility is maintained.\n1173\t\n1174\t10. **Events table for history**: Every mutation records an event row. `bf log` queries the events table — O(1) by issue ID. Long-term history via git log on `issues.jsonl`.\n1175\t\n1176\t11. **Secret scanning before write**: Built-in regex-based secret detection prevents credentials from entering SQLite or the JSONL export. Configurable patterns, git pre-commit hook integration.\n1177\t\n1178\t12. **`.beads/` is committed to git**: `issues.jsonl` + config are version-controlled. `beads.db` is gitignored (binary, rebuilt from JSONL on `bf sync --import`). Secret scanning protects the exported JSONL.\n1179\t\n1180\t13. **Critical path drives claim priority, not just listed priority**: Listed priority is a human signal, but it decays as the project evolves and humans stop curating it. Critical path float is computed from the live dependency graph and is always current. A priority-3 bead on the critical path outranks a priority-0 bead with float=5 — the fleet naturally works on what matters most without human recuration.\n1181\t\n1182\t14. **Worker composition is first-class metadata**: `--model`, `--harness`, `--harness-version` on `bf claim` record what kind of agent did the work. This transforms the events table from a bare audit log into a performance dataset: which model+harness combinations close which task types fastest. The fleet becomes self-optimizing — velocity data informs which workers to dispatch to which workspace, without any external ML pipeline.\n1183\t\n1184\t---\n1185\t\n1186\t## Alternative Approaches Considered\n1187\t\n1188\t### In-Memory Server (deferred)\n1189\t\n1190\tThe plan originally included a coordination server: persistent process, Unix socket protocol, `Arc<Mutex<ServerState>>`, in-memory BTreeMap priority queues, heartbeat-based stale detection. This was deferred to a future optimization because SQLite `BEGIN IMMEDIATE` delivers sufficient throughput at current scale.\n1191\t\n1192\tThe server would reduce per-claim latency from ~2ms (SQLite transaction) to ~0.1ms (memory pop). This matters only if fleets exceed 50 workers or claim frequency exceeds ~500/sec — neither is on the horizon. The server can be added transparently: `bf claim` detects the server socket, delegates if present, falls back to SQLite if not.\n1193\t\n1194\t### MCP Agent Mail (Dicklesworthstone/mcp_agent_mail_rust)\n1195\t\n1196\tJeffrey Emanuel's companion system for inter-agent coordination. A Rust MCP server with 36 tools, 33 resources, Git-backed archive, SQLite indexing, HTTP/TUI/Robot surfaces.\n1197\t\n1198\t**Architecture**: Agents register identities, claim file reservations with TTL, exchange threaded messages, negotiate work assignments via acknowledgements. Coordination happens through conversation — \"I'm taking src/auth/**, can you work on tests/?\"\n1199\t\n1200\t**Why it doesn't fit bead-forge**: Agent Mail is built for the **pets** model — named, persistent agents that maintain identity across sessions, negotiate via messaging, and coordinate through conversation. NEEDLE uses the **cattle** model — disposable workers that are interchangeable, stateless, and need atomic dequeue without any conversation.\n1201\t\n1202\t| Aspect | Agent Mail (Pets) | bead-forge (Cattle) |\n1203\t|--------|-------------------|---------------------|\n1204\t| Agent identity | Registered, named, persistent | Anonymous, stateless, disposable |\n1205\t| Work assignment | Negotiation, messaging, agreement | Atomic SQL dequeue (BEGIN IMMEDIATE) |\n1206\t| Coordination mechanism | Threaded messages, acknowledgements | Kernel-provided mutual exclusion |\n1207\t| File/workspace ownership | Advisory file reservations | None — beads are the unit of work |\n1208\t| Communication pattern | Multi-turn conversation | Single CLI invocation |\n1209\t| Failure mode | Agent re-joins conversation | Agent dies, claim TTL expires, bead reopens |\n1210\t| Agent count | Small (3-5 named agents) | Large fleet (11-20+ disposable workers) |\n1211\t\n1212\t**What to borrow from Agent Mail**:\n1213\t- **TTL-based claim expiration**: Agent Mail uses TTL on file reservations. bead-forge applies the same concept — claims older than `claim_ttl` are reclaimed to `open` on the next claim invocation.\n1214\t\n1215\t**What to explicitly reject**:\n1216\t- **Agent identities**: Workers don't register or maintain identity. The `--assignee` field is for logging, not identity.\n1217\t- **Messaging/threading**: Workers don't send messages to each other. The only communication is claim/close through the JSONL file.\n1218\t- **File reservations**: Workers operate on entire beads, not file-level reservations.\n1219\t- **MCP layer**: bead-forge is a CLI. No stdio-based MCP protocol.\n1220\t- **Advisory locks**: Claims are enforced by `BEGIN IMMEDIATE`, not advisory. Once claimed (inside the transaction), no other worker sees that bead as open.\n1221\t\n1222\t### BeadHub (juanre/beadhub)\n1223\t\n1224\tA coordination server for AI agent teams built on top of Steve Yegge's Dolt-based `bd`. The `bdh` CLI wraps `bd` and adds work claiming, file reservation, presence awareness, and inter-agent messaging. Includes a web dashboard.\n1225\t\n1226\t**Why it doesn't fit**: Tied to Dolt-based `bd` architecture (not JSONL). bead-forge needs JSONL+SQLite compatibility with br, not Dolt compatibility with bd. However, the coordination server concept validates that this problem is real and worth solving.\n1227\t\n1228\t### Beads Viewer (Dicklesworthstone/beads_viewer)\n1229\t\n1230\tGraph-aware TUI with PageRank-based prioritization, critical path analysis, and kanban board view.\n1231\t\n1232\t**Why it doesn't fit**: Read-only visualization tool. Cannot perform writes (claiming, status changes). The PageRank and critical path concepts are interesting for future prioritization but don't solve the concurrency problem.\n1233\t"}]},"parent_tool_use_id":null,"session_id":"90b2955e-05b1-45f7-ba6b-37b4628c1cba","uuid":"4f6fd03d-cd0e-45de-b1bd-c95865f65883","timestamp":"2026-04-29T23:21:48.174Z","tool_use_result":{"type":"text","file":{"filePath":"/home/coding/bead-forge/docs/plan/plan.md","content":"# bead-forge Implementation Plan\n\n## Overview\n\n**bead-forge** (`bf`) is a Rust binary that replaces `br` (beads_rust). SQLite is the live database — all reads and writes go through it. `issues.jsonl` is a git-synced artifact exported on demand: one entry per bead, committed to the repo for backup, sharing, and recovery. Concurrent claiming is handled by SQLite's `BEGIN IMMEDIATE` transaction — no server, no daemon, no flock required.\n\n## Core Principles\n\n1. **SQLite is the live store** — all mutations are SQL writes; reads are SQL queries. Fast, concurrent-read, serialized-write via WAL mode.\n2. **JSONL is the git artifact** — exported on `bf sync`, committed to git, one entry per bead. Used for backup, cross-machine sharing, and recovery. Never written during normal operation.\n3. **Drop-in CLI** — all `br` commands work under `bf` with the same flags and output formats\n4. **`BEGIN IMMEDIATE` for atomic claim** — the read-score-update sequence runs inside a single SQLite write transaction, eliminating the race condition `br` has without requiring flock or a daemon\n\n---\n\n## Phase 1: Core Library — Data Model & JSONL Import/Export\n\n### 1.1 Data Model (`src/model.rs`)\n\nPort the exact `Issue`, `Status`, `Priority`, `IssueType`, `Dependency`, `DependencyType`, `Comment`, and `Event` structs from beads_rust with identical Serde attributes. This is the wire format — every field, every `skip_serializing_if`, every rename must match.\n\nKey structs and their JSONL serialization:\n\n```\nStatus:       open | in_progress | blocked | deferred | draft | closed | tombstone | pinned | Custom(String)\nPriority:     transparent i32 (0=Critical, 4=Backlog)\nIssueType:    task | bug | feature | epic | chore | docs | question | Custom(String)\nDependency:   { issue_id, depends_on_id, type (renamed from dep_type), created_at, created_by?, metadata?, thread_id? }\nComment:      { id: i64, issue_id, author, text (renamed from body), created_at }\nEvent:        { id: i64, issue_id, event_type, actor, old_value?, new_value?, comment?, created_at }\n```\n\nIssue fields (alphabetical by JSON key):\n```\nid, title, description?, design?, acceptance_criteria?, notes?,\nstatus, priority, issue_type, assignee?, owner?, estimated_minutes?,\ncreated_at, created_by?, updated_at, closed_at?, close_reason?,\nclosed_by_session?, due_at?, defer_until?, external_ref?,\nsource_system?, source_repo, deleted_at?, deleted_by?, delete_reason?,\noriginal_type?, compaction_level (default 0), compacted_at?,\ncompacted_at_commit?, original_size?, sender?, ephemeral (default false),\npinned (default false), is_template (default false),\nlabels: Vec<String>, dependencies: Vec<Dependency>, comments: Vec<Comment>\n```\n\n### 1.2 JSONL Import (`src/jsonl.rs`)\n\nJSONL is read only during `bf sync --import` (pulling state from git) and `bf doctor --repair` (rebuilding SQLite from the artifact). Never read during normal CLI operation.\n\n```rust\nfn import_jsonl(jsonl_path: &Path, storage: &Storage) -> Result<ImportResult> {\n    let file = File::open(jsonl_path)?;\n    let reader = BufReader::new(file);\n    storage.with_write_transaction(|tx| {\n        for line in reader.lines() {\n            let issue: Issue = serde_json::from_str(&line?)?;\n            tx.upsert_issue(&issue)?;\n        }\n        Ok(())\n    })\n}\n```\n\nFunctions:\n- `import_jsonl(path, storage)` — bulk upsert from JSONL into SQLite\n- `stream_issues(path) -> impl Iterator<Item = Result<Issue>>` — lazy line iterator (used by import and doctor)\n\n### 1.3 JSONL Export (`src/jsonl.rs`)\n\nJSONL is written only during `bf sync --flush` (preparing the git artifact). Exports current bead state from SQLite, one entry per bead, sorted by ID for stable diffs. Atomic temp+rename.\n\n```rust\nfn export_jsonl(jsonl_path: &Path, storage: &Storage) -> Result<ExportResult> {\n    let issues = storage.list_all_issues()?;  // sorted by ID\n    let temp_path = jsonl_path.with_extension(\"jsonl.tmp\");\n    let mut writer = BufWriter::new(File::create_new(&temp_path)?);\n    for issue in &issues {\n        serde_json::to_writer(&mut writer, issue)?;\n        writer.write_all(b\"\\n\")?;\n    }\n    writer.flush()?;\n    drop(writer);\n    fs::rename(&temp_path, jsonl_path)?;\n    Ok(ExportResult { count: issues.len() })\n}\n```\n\nFunctions:\n- `export_jsonl(path, storage)` — dump all beads from SQLite to JSONL (atomic)\n- `export_jsonl_dirty(path, storage)` — export only dirty beads (incremental, faster for large workspaces)\n\n### 1.4 Config (`src/config.rs`)\n\nParse `.beads/config.yaml` with the same fields br uses:\n\n```yaml\nissue_prefixes: [bd, fg]\ndefault_priority: 2\ndefault_type: task\nscoring:\n  priority_weight: 0.4\n  blockers_weight: 0.3\n  age_weight: 0.2\n  labels_weight: 0.1\n  max_age_hours: 20\n  max_blockers: 3\n# bead-forge additions (additive, br ignores these)\nclaim_ttl_minutes: 30\n```\n\nParse `.beads/metadata.json`:\n```json\n{ \"database\": \"beads.db\", \"jsonl_export\": \"issues.jsonl\" }\n```\n\n### 1.5 ID Generation (`src/id.rs`)\n\nPort br's ID scheme: `<prefix>-<hash>` where hash is base36 lowercase. Use the birthday-problem adaptive length (3-8 chars). Read `issue_prefixes` from config (first entry is the default prefix).\n\n```rust\nfn generate_id(prefix: &str, existing_count: usize) -> String {\n    let len = optimal_hash_length(existing_count);\n    let random_bytes = rand::random::<[u8; 16]>();\n    let hash = sha256(&random_bytes);\n    base36_encode(&hash[..len])\n    format!(\"{}-{}\", prefix, hash)\n}\n```\n\n---\n\n## Phase 2: SQLite Primary Store\n\n### 2.1 Schema Application (`src/storage/schema.rs`)\n\nApply the exact same `CREATE TABLE IF NOT EXISTS` DDL from br's `SCHEMA_SQL`. Tables:\n\n| Table | Purpose |\n|-------|---------|\n| `issues` | All 35 columns, same types, defaults, CHECK constraints |\n| `dependencies` | (issue_id, depends_on_id) PK, type, metadata, thread_id |\n| `labels` | (issue_id, label) PK |\n| `comments` | AUTOINCREMENT id, issue_id, author, text, created_at |\n| `events` | AUTOINCREMENT id, issue_id, event_type, actor, old/new/comment |\n| `config` | key-value |\n| `metadata` | key-value |\n| `dirty_issues` | Track which issues need JSONL export |\n| `export_hashes` | Incremental export tracking |\n| `blocked_issues_cache` | Materialized view of blocked issues |\n| `child_counters` | Hierarchical IDs (bd-abc.1, bd-abc.2) |\n| `recovery_sessions` | Anomaly/recovery audit trail |\n| `anomaly_audit` | Recovery event tracking |\n\nAll indexes from br must be created identically, including the critical `idx_issues_ready` composite partial index.\n\n### 2.2 Storage Engine (`src/storage/sqlite.rs`)\n\nUse `rusqlite` (not FrankenSQLite) bundled with system SQLite. Apply WAL mode, foreign keys, busy_timeout=30s, cache_size=-8000, synchronous=NORMAL.\n\nAll mutations go through here. JSONL is never touched during normal operation.\n\nFunctions:\n- `open(path: &Path) -> Result<Storage>` — open/create DB, apply schema\n- `get_issue(id: &str) -> Result<Option<Issue>>` — point lookup by ID\n- `list_issues(filter: IssueFilter) -> Result<Vec<Issue>>` — filtered query with WHERE clauses\n- `list_all_issues() -> Result<Vec<Issue>>` — full table scan sorted by ID (for JSONL export)\n- `create_issue(issue: &Issue) -> Result<()>` — INSERT\n- `update_issue(id: &str, changes: IssueChanges) -> Result<()>` — UPDATE + mark dirty\n- `close_issue(id: &str, reason: &str) -> Result<()>` — status transition + mark dirty\n- `with_write_transaction(f) -> Result<T>` — execute closure in a write transaction\n- `with_immediate_transaction(f) -> Result<T>` — `BEGIN IMMEDIATE` with retry (see §2.5) — acquires write lock before any reads (used by claim)\n- `rebuild_blocked_cache() -> Result<()>` — recalculate blocked issues materialized view\n\n### 2.3 Sync Protocol (`src/sync.rs`)\n\nPort br's sync semantics:\n\n**Flush (SQLite → JSONL, for git)**:\n1. Call `export_jsonl_dirty` — query dirty bead IDs, export full current state of each from SQLite\n2. Atomic temp+rename over `issues.jsonl`\n3. Clear `dirty_issues`, update `export_hashes`\n\nFor `bf sync` (full flush): call `export_jsonl` — dump all beads sorted by ID, unconditionally.\n\n**Import (JSONL → SQLite, from git pull)**:\n1. Stream `issues.jsonl` line by line\n2. Compare each with SQLite state using `content_hash`\n3. INSERT new, UPDATE changed, SKIP unchanged\n4. Handle collisions (same ID, different content) with deterministic resolution\n\n### 2.5 Concurrent Write Safety (`src/storage/sqlite.rs`)\n\nSQLite WAL mode serializes concurrent writers through a single write lock — they queue, not corrupt. `SQLITE_BUSY` is returned when a writer cannot acquire the lock within `busy_timeout`. With claim latency of ~1-2ms and a 20-worker fleet, the entire queue clears in ~20-40ms, so `SQLITE_BUSY` should never occur in normal operation. However, a retry wrapper is the cheap safety net that makes this a guarantee rather than an assumption:\n\n```rust\nconst MAX_RETRIES: u32 = 5;\nconst RETRY_BASE_MS: u64 = 50;\n\nfn with_immediate_transaction<T>(\n    conn: &Connection,\n    f: impl Fn(&Transaction) -> Result<T>,\n) -> Result<T> {\n    let mut attempt = 0;\n    loop {\n        match conn.execute(\"BEGIN IMMEDIATE\", []) {\n            Ok(_) => {\n                let tx = conn.unchecked_transaction()?;\n                return match f(&tx) {\n                    Ok(val) => { tx.commit()?; Ok(val) }\n                    Err(e) => { let _ = tx.rollback(); Err(e) }\n                };\n            }\n            Err(e) if is_busy_error(&e) && attempt < MAX_RETRIES => {\n                attempt += 1;\n                std::thread::sleep(Duration::from_millis(RETRY_BASE_MS * attempt as u64));\n                continue;\n            }\n            Err(e) => return Err(e.into()),\n        }\n    }\n}\n\nfn is_busy_error(e: &rusqlite::Error) -> bool {\n    matches!(\n        e,\n        rusqlite::Error::SqliteFailure(\n            rusqlite::ffi::Error { code: rusqlite::ErrorCode::DatabaseBusy, .. },\n            _\n        )\n    )\n}\n```\n\n**Why this is sufficient and not a workaround**: `SQLITE_BUSY` with WAL mode is not data corruption — it is a clean \"lock unavailable, try again\" signal. The database is fully consistent when this occurs. The retry converts a transient contention spike (e.g., 20 workers all starting within the same millisecond) into a short wait rather than a user-visible error.\n\n**All write operations** (`claim`, `create`, `update`, `close`, `batch`) use `with_immediate_transaction`. Read-only operations (`list`, `show`, `ready`) use a plain `BEGIN DEFERRED` transaction and are never affected by write contention.\n\n### 2.7 Doctor/Repair (`src/doctor.rs`)\n\n- `doctor --repair`: Delete `beads.db`, reimport from JSONL\n- `doctor --check`: Validate JSONL line integrity, check SQLite <-> JSONL consistency\n- Recovery from corruption: JSONL export is always authoritative — `beads.db` can be rebuilt from it at any time\n\n---\n\n## Phase 3: CLI Commands\n\n### 3.1 Command Structure (`src/cli/`)\n\nUse `clap` with derive macros. Binary name: `bf`. Subcommands mirror br exactly.\n\n```\nbf create    --title \"...\" --type <type> --priority <N> [--description \"...\"] [--label ...]\nbf list      [--status <s>] [--type <t>] [--assignee <a>] [--limit N] [--format json|text|toon]\nbf show      <id>\nbf update    <id> [--status <s>] [--assignee <a>] [--priority <N>] [--title \"...\"] ...\nbf close     <id> [--reason \"...\"]\nbf reopen    <id>\nbf delete    <id>\nbf ready         [--limit N]                     # unblocked, open, sorted by priority\nbf claim         --assignee <id>                 # atomic claim (see Phase 4)\n                 [--model <model>]               # e.g. claude-sonnet-4-6\n                 [--harness <name>]              # e.g. needle\n                 [--harness-version <ver>]       # e.g. 0.5.2\n                 [--workspace <path>] [--any]\nbf critical-path <epic-id>                       # show critical path + float for each bead\nbf dep           add-blocker <parent> <child>\nbf dep           remove-blocker <parent> <child>\nbf dep           tree <id>\nbf label         <id> add <label>\nbf label         <id> remove <label>\nbf comment       <id> [--author <a>] [--text \"...\"]\nbf sync          --flush-only\nbf sync          --import-only\nbf doctor        [--repair]\nbf init          [--prefix <p>]\nbf stats\nbf count         [--status <s>]\nbf search        <query>\nbf schema\nbf config        get <key>\nbf config        set <key> <value>\n```\n\n### 3.2 Output Formats\n\nThree formats, matching br exactly:\n- **text**: Human-readable table (default for terminal)\n- **json**: One JSON object per line (for piping)\n- **toon**: Token-optimized output for LLM context windows\n\n### 3.3 Execution Model\n\nEach command:\n1. Locate `.beads/` directory (walk up from CWD)\n2. Load config + metadata\n3. Open SQLite (`beads.db`), apply schema if new\n4. Execute: mutations are SQL writes; reads are SQL queries\n5. `bf sync` is the only command that touches `issues.jsonl` — flush exports it, import reads it\n\n---\n\n## Phase 4: Concurrent Claiming\n\n### 4.1 Architecture: SQLite `BEGIN IMMEDIATE`\n\nThe thundering herd problem — N workers racing to claim the same bead — is solved by running the entire read-score-update sequence inside a single `BEGIN IMMEDIATE` transaction. SQLite's write lock is acquired before any reads, so no two workers can read the same candidate state. No flock, no server, no daemon.\n\n```\nWorker 1: BEGIN IMMEDIATE → SELECT candidates → score → UPDATE winner → COMMIT\nWorker 2: BEGIN IMMEDIATE → (blocked at write lock until Worker 1 COMMITs) → SELECT → score → UPDATE → COMMIT\nWorker 3: BEGIN IMMEDIATE → (blocked) → ...\n...\nWorker 20: BEGIN IMMEDIATE → (blocked) → SELECT → NONE (queue empty) → COMMIT (no-op)\n```\n\nEach claim is a single CLI invocation. The critical section (lock held) is: SELECT scoring fields → score in memory → UPDATE winner + stale resets → COMMIT. Lock held for ~0.5-2ms.\n\n**Throughput**: SQLite handles claims purely in memory after the initial page cache warm-up:\n\n| Workspace | Active beads | Claim latency | Throughput |\n|-----------|-------------|---------------|-----------|\n| Typical (FORGE) | 248 | ~0.5ms | ~2000/sec |\n| Medium (NEEDLE) | 518 | ~1ms | ~1000/sec |\n| Large | 2000 | ~2ms | ~500/sec |\n\nWith 20 workers claiming simultaneously, the last worker waits ~20-40ms (19 queued transactions × ~1-2ms each). The fleet needs ~1-2 claims/sec at steady state — SQLite is overkill by 3 orders of magnitude.\n\n### 4.2 Atomic Claim (`src/claim.rs`)\n\nThe entire claim sequence runs inside a single `BEGIN IMMEDIATE` transaction. SQLite acquires the write lock before any reads, so no two workers can observe the same candidate state.\n\n```rust\nfn claim(storage: &Storage, worker: &str, claim_ttl: Duration) -> Result<Option<Issue>> {\n    storage.with_immediate_transaction(|tx| {\n        let now = Utc::now();\n\n        // 1. Reclaim stale in_progress beads\n        tx.execute(\n            \"UPDATE issues SET status='open', assignee=NULL, updated_at=?1\n             WHERE status='in_progress' AND updated_at < ?2\",\n            params![now, now - claim_ttl],\n        )?;\n\n        // 2.
